text:
My husband -- who hates chicken with an unnatural passion the likes of which one only expects to encounter in relation to the usual suspects: anchovies, liver, random Kardashians, and the like -- THAT guy had this to say of this recipe: "Wow. That's good chicken. And you know it pains me to say that." And THEN, my 11 y.o. kid ate an unprecedented THREE servings of a non-dessert-related dish. It was like I won the Mom Olympics tonight. Got recruited on the Chinese team and plain won that thing. Many thanks for the recipe. I didn't have the fancy Chinese chili, so I used run-of-the-mill chili powder. Also, I put a broil on the last few minutes to give it a bit of edge. Apparently, it was all magic.

text:
This is my new go-to meal to cook when I am delivering a meal to someone else.  I make it with brown rice (throw in a couple of chicken bouillon cubes with the rice water and finish with fresh parsley.  I use chicken thigh fillets--skinless and boneless.  I also have made this so often that I don't waste the precious sauce by marinating the meat at all!  I baste the meat a few times and save the yummy asian sauce to drizzle over the rice.  This is seriously the best chicken recipe I've ever made! Enjoy!

text:
NO need to double the sauce, just reserve the marinate and pour into a sauce pan making sure you boil 5 minutes.  Use some cornstarch to thicken if needed. Spoon 1/3 of the sauce over the chicken before baking. No need to discard the marinate when you can just use as the sauce.  Also can cut back on the Sesame oil ( I used slightly less than 1/4 cup). Did not find this very spicy.  I marinated in the fridge for 24 hours and yum the meat really absorbed the flavor. Popped it in the oven the following night and it was a fast and easy meal. Used legs and thighs that I skinned removing as much fat as I could. Just make sure you bring the sauce back to a boil for 1 to 2 minutes after chicken is done. There will be sauce from the cooked chicken left in the casserole dish which you can use for extra sauce. Served it over sticky rice with green peas.  Will definately make again. Thank you for a delicious recipe Essanaye.

text:
Just made this tonight, and it turned out pretty nicely. It is quite spicy, so if you're spice-phobic, you can cut it in half. Not sure if it was the particular oil I used, but it's flavor overpowered the other ingredients in the marinade so I would recommend a bit less or non-toasted oil. I also cooked the marinade longer on very low heat while the chicken was in the oven so it could caramelize a bit more. Used drumsticks and thighs. Yum!

text:
Amazing!!!  The only change I made was to reduce the oil by half - because its such a strong flavor.  I cut up 6 chicken breasts into small pieces and marinated for the night.  I transferred chicken to a frying pan with a slotted spoon and cooked it on high.  I made a second batch of marinade and boiled that in a pan.  I then added some cornstarch/water mix to the marinade to thicken.  Once the chicken started to brown, I poured the marinade over it and let it simmer for 5 mins.  Served over rice ---- AMAZING!  Thanks for sharing this.

This was absolutely FANTASTIC.  Chicken fell apart tenderly, the sauce taste was amazing.  I know how folks on this site don't care for folks to "add their own twist" to recipes, and I agree... but, in this instance, I was out of a couple of ingredients so I subbed other items and it still turned out great. text:
I made this, simplifying it quite a bit.  I skipped marinating this altogether.  I made half of the marinade, heating it on the stovetop and then thickening it with a water/cornstarch slurry, just enough to give it some nice body.  Hubs grilled boneless skinless chicken breast halves, and used the thickened marinade as a basting sauce, which worked beautifully.  This was so much simpler than making the recipe as written.  I would make it again the same way.  I served this with Sesame Noodle Salad, also from this site.

Like others, I thought there was way too much sesame oil so I only added a few drops. I decided to marinate this longer so I left out the vinegar and marinated for a few hours. I scored the chicken thighs with a knife to let the marinade seep in. I added the vinegar when I made the sauce on the stove, and cooked the marinade from the chicken as well. I used far less chili oil as my kids were eating this, so we just served it with hot sauce on the side for us adults! My husband and I loved it, my picky kids not so much but they ate most of it! ;) I think next time I'll add a bit of ginger since I left out most of the chili oil, to make even more delish!

text:
I read the description, and got a bit worried about the combination, But it was terrific. Hubby, who hates spicy, loved it. Son, who hates thighs, chowed down. I'm glad I didn't mess with the ingredients. 

A few notes, though, for newbie cooks. Thighs are a bit fatty. Take the time to cut off the fat (as much as possible) and extra skin, if you keep it on. I used a roaster pan, and put a wire rack in it, to keep the drippings away as the chicken cooked. Make sure to spray some nonstick oil on it, or you'll be cleaning up for hours. 

I brushed the marinade on every 10 minutes, mostly because I liked the taste. I did thicken it with cornstarch first. After the 30 minutes were up, I set the oven to 450 degrees, and toasted the top of the marinade covered skin. 

Voila. Incredibly tasty and moist chicken.

I made the sauce and was sad to find out that it required nearly the same ingredients as a teryaki sauce I made in the past and did NOT like.  Although I had to substitute 5tbs of Honey with 3tbs of... Pancake Syrup and I didn't have the garlic/chili paste so I substituted 1-2tbs of chili powder. text:
I think the ingredients as to "Asian Chili Garlic Sauce" could be more clear, as it's pretty generic and many Asian cultures have a version of chili garlic sauce. What does that mean? Korean Gochujang? Sriracha? or Sweet Thai Chili sauce? I have all three and I assumed the recipe called for Siriracha, because it is the most common of the three. This was the wrong choice. It was much too spicy, and I tolerate spice pretty well. I think the Sweet Thai Chili sauce or even the Gochujang was the route to go. So those of you wondering, unless you're obsessed with Sriracha, go with the Sweet Thai Chili sauce.

text:
Nice outcome for little work, definitely a "keeper". Made twice now, with changes due to comments, pantry and a 1st try. It's very easy to tweak the spice level for your own heat tolerance. We (a hot family) didn't think it was hot. IMO, the most critical change is to marinate longer if you can; 1 hour didn't do much, but 4+ is great. We don't like a lot of oil, so I reduced that to 2 TBSP, and I didn't have sesame oil so I used 1 TBSP sesame seeds the first time (okay), and tahini the second (really good). I did need to add some flour to thicken the sauce to my liking. I added clementine orange sections to the garnish the 2nd time which I'll do again. Yum!

text:
This was excellent.   Didn't change ingredients except for using bone in legs and thighs.   Put chicken and marinade in sprayed baking dish.  Baked 30 minutes, then added some glaze on top and baked an additional 20 minutes as was suggested by another reviewer.  With remaining mixture, I microwaved it in glass bowl about 2 minutes, stirred, and cooked about another 2 minutes until thickened.  When chicken was done, I removed the pieces  to a plate, poured the pan juices in with microwaved sauce.  Stirred and heated up to a boil, then added 3 T. of cornstarch that was mixed with about 1//4 cup cold water.  Poured cornstarch mixture in, stirred, then microwaved about a minute and it thickened up nicely.  I placed chicken back in dish and poured sauce mixture over all.  Sorry this is wordy, thought it may be a help to someone.  We loved it.

text:
Very nice flavor. I used it on chicken thighs that I baked in the oven and they turned out fantastic. I made one change, which I do with any chicken recipe, and that is to cover the dish with foil for the first 1/3-1/2 time of baking and uncover for the rest. Use a thermometer to check the temperature and if it's not quite cooked all the way then leave it in for a few more minutes until it is. The chicken is always juicy on the inside and never burnt on the outside.

text:
I used this marinate on chicken thighs. I put the thighs and half the marinate in a qt. food saver bag and sealed it. I put it in the refrigerator for about 2 hours and turn it over once. With the other half of marinate I reduced it down until it thickened. We grilled the thighs. We loved the flavor of the chicken and the thickened sauce was great, we spooned it over the chicken. This will be my go to marinate for chicken. May try it on pork chops.

OH MY!   This is my first ever recipe review.  This recipe deserves a review and all 5 stars!

text:
Even though I didn't have all the ingredients or the time to marinade overnight, this turned out to be a really great dish!! Substituted apple cider vinegar for the rice vinegar, & used vegetable oil for the sesame oil. Use slightly less Apple cider vinegar as it is stronger than rice vinegar (I started with 1/4 c then added a small bit at a time to my taste). I marinated for one hour, then instead of throwing out the marinade I thickened it a bit with some cornstarch, then basted the chicken with it every 15 mins until done. Hubby, who hates anything vinegar-y, LOVED this dish, & even used the extra sauce on his rice. Served it with 7-grain rice steamed in chicken broth per the suggestion of a previous reviewer, & added an Asian-style cold slaw on the side. Will definitely make this dish again when I have the proper ingredients & the time to marinade overnight, it can only make this dish even better! Thanks for helping me find something my hubby likes that isn't steak & potatoes!!

I made this putting all the marinade in with the chicken then transferred it all into a pot to cook. I used 1/2 the sesame oil called for and 2 instead of 3 tbls of sriracha chili sauce (hubby a bit heat sensitive).  Put about a 1/2 cup marinade under the chicken (used large chunks of breasts) and basted and turned several times while baking.  Lastly threw under broiler to get a good sear.  We all loved this dish served with wild rice and broccoli.  Thanks for the recipe!

city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
Turned out very good with a few adjustments. First off, I will reduce the amount of sesame oil next time because it's too strong with a 1/4 cup - maybe no more than 2 Tbsp. I also omitted the salt. Before marinating the boneless, skinless chicken thighs, I seasoned them with a bit of garlic powder and Schezwan seasoning. After tasting the marinade, I thought it needed a little more flavor so I added a few dashes of fish sauce and a bit more soy sauce. I marinated the chicken overnight but agree with another reviewer, you don't need to use half, just enough to cover the chicken and use the rest for basting instead. I cooked for about 40 minutes (30 minutes will do - I was multitasking). I basted the chicken every 10 minutes. Halfway through cooking, I drained the extra juices out of the pan because I prefer it without the extra juice, just the flavor. Didn't have time to stir fry rice so I made rice with peas and carrots and added some of the marinade to it. Quick and delicious meal. Next time I'll try it on the grill.

text:
These chicken thighs were delicious.  I did tweak the recipe a bit.  Instead of 1/4 cup of sesame oil, I just used 3 Tbs.  Sometimes I feel sesame oil can be quite potent.  I didn't want it to overtake the dish.  I used sriracha as my chili garlic sauce.  I also did not add any salt because of the sodium in the soy sauce.  I let them marinate for around 5 hours.  I did let them bake for 45 minutes so they would get to 165 degrees on the meat thermometer.  My family does not usually like thighs, especially my husband, but he raved about this recipe.  I will definitely make this recipe again and often.

text:
How is this for a replacement?: I didn't have chicken thighs, which I'm sure would be great, but I did have pork steaks, so why not? Also I used Huy Fong Sriracha as a stand-in for Asian garlic sauce. I love garlic so much that I had to up the ante by adding  a few hacked up good sized cloves and while I was at it, about 1/3 cup chopped white onion which I threw in because I needed to use it or lose it. Sorry, I can't let a perfectly good onion go to waste. Instead of an hour, I marinaded overnight and I cooked them on open foil in their marinade on my Weber Kettle at 350 indirect cooking method using Kingsford blue bag charcoal for fuel and maple and apple wood chunks for smoke. I cooked them to medium rare and then used direct heat over the cooler part of the coals for a few minutes to bring them up to medium using an instant read thermometer, flipping and basting with thickened sauce often to avoid burning the sugar and to get a nice even sear on both sides. I served these with basmati rice and grilled asparagus drizzled with my homemade garlic and red, white and black cracked peppercorn infused olive oil and flaked sea salt. I also served the thickened marinade on the side as a dipping sauce for the meat. Dee-lish! I definitely will make this again.

I added a tablespoon of minced ginger to the marinade. I poured all of the marinade in the bag and once finished I just put it in a small sauce pan. I added 2 table spoons of brown sugar to the sauce as it was coming to a boil. Also hot Chinese mustard goes great with the chicken as a condiment. ;) 4 stars since I changed it. 5 stars for my own. Lol

text:
So... first of all, the chicken came out amazing. My mom suggested I even make it for my coworkers next time there's a potluck. (FYI I'm a semi new cook, learning as I go) Secondly, I made a few changes to this recipe. It calls for garlic cloves, which I did not have so I used garlic powder. I also used low sodium soy sauce and didn't include the full amount because I'm not a fan of the taste. This recipe also called for sesame oil and rice vinegar which I also don't have, so I followed another reviewer's idea and used apple cider vinegar., and instead of sesame oil I used Trader Joe's Garlic infused Olive Oil (which I absolutely LOVE). Now on to what I didn't like and how I fixed it. While my chicken was cooking in the over and the sauce was already made, I tasted and was disappointed at how much it tasted like soy sauce (mind you I already didn't use the required amount). So I looked around my kitchen and found hickory smoked bbq sauce and poured about a tablespoon in and mixed it up, PERFECT. Lastly, I didn't really feel like cutting up green onions, so I opted for parsley instead. Overall I loved this dish with the minor changes that I made. Def gonna make it again. *adds to list of MUST MAKE AGAIN recipes* lol

text:
This was pretty tasty, but I did find I had to make some changes to the recipe as written. First, as some other reviews have stated, the sesame oil needs to be much less, it's a very strong flavor and you need only about half as much as this recipe calls for because it's overpowering. Secondly, the sauce never really "thickened" like it was supposed to. I boiled the sauce for almost twice as long as instructed and had no thickening. It didn't change the flavor in any way, but it did make "basting" strange, since the sauce slid off the meat. But overall, it was a very tasty recipe, and I would definitely make it again with some modifications.

text:
Really easy recipe very spicy and delicious.  A perfect recipe for people who love spicy food.  I did modify the recipe a bit because I was cooking this for young kids.  After tasting the sauce I realized that it was too spicy for the kids.  I had already used half of sauce to marinade the chicken.  I have to admit I panicked.  So I added more honey and some sugar and kept tasting it as I was modifying it.  I added about a teaspoon of hoisin sauce.  I did all of this as I was simmering the remainder of the sauce and the sauce came out really good.  I baked the chicken with the skin on.  I served the chicken with rice and removed the skin and the kids loved it.  I will definitely make this again.

Delicious... although I did make quite a few adjustments to up the heat factor and give it a kick while keeping the base similar. Added about 5 tbs of Sriracha, changed the rice vinegar to Apple Cider vinegar (it's what I had in the pantry but it turned out great) added some Hoisin sauce and cut WAY back on the sesame oil to just 2 tbs...the flavor of it was just too strong with the original amount and seemed to overpower everything. I've made these a few times now and they're a big hit. I also like to sear them in a cast iron skillet before I throw them in the oven and then baste the remaining marinade over them every 7-10 mins while cooking.

This was my first complex meat dish for a school project. I'm a huge fan of Asian cuisine and basically eat it all the time. This dish was defiantly something else. (By something else, I mean, A+, haha) it's defiantly delightful! I added some stuff of my own. I added in onion salt and garlic powder in the sauce, not a lot, but just enough to give it some extra flavor. I also added apple cider vinagar. It gives the chicken a lovely sweet taste. I skipped out on added minced garlic and Asian chili garlic sauce, because I was either really really low on it or didn't have any. But it honestly turned out great without it! I would also recommend grilling some nicely diced onions with herbs  and chopped up chives. Along with olive oil while grilling. Also while the chicken was cooking, I would pour vinegar and the juices from the chicken onto the chicken to make it juicer. Also boiled eggs are a nice side to the dish! Thank you so much for the recipe and hopefully you might try my little tips! Very good dish! ;u;

This has become a family favorite for my two boys, 2 and 3, and my wife. 

I don't bother marinating and the chicken is plenty flavorful. 

I also skip the chili, the boys aren't ready for heat quite yet. 

I pour on both sides and cook smooth side up for 1st 10 minutes. I then pour on both sides again and cook the final 20 minutes bottom side up so the sauce bakes deep into the chicken. 

I also like to mince a bit more garlic than the recipe asks for. 

Serve with rice and broccoli and you have smiling faces.

text:
I would love to have been able to follow this recipe, but I was missing one key ingredient - the Chili Garlic Sauce. But I had everything else. So I used one TBSP of Chili Oil just to get the Chili flavor in there. In preparation for doing something with these lovely Chix Thighs, I had bought some Ginger Root. So, as I had that on hand, I added about 1 TBSP of grated Fresh Ginger Root to the marinade/basting sauce.

We have some blood pressure issues in our household, so I just skipped the salt. No one at the table picked up the salt grinder!

Oh, and I had gone searching for recipes to GRILL. So how this recipe came up is a mystery. Nonetheless, I consulted with my household grillmeister, and he said, "Fine for the Grill!" 

And it was! I split the marinade as directed and we used the extra sauce, boiled down a bit, for basting on the grill (charcoal).

Our 15-year old grandson is visiting, and he actually complimented both of us on our dinner preparation and thanked us for a delicious meal as we were picking up. Can't go wrong with that kind of review!

Oh and the leftover sauce was great on the plain rice we served as a starch. 

Definitely on our list of keepers for regular meals!

text:
I made two double batches of sauce for a double recipe of chicken. The first one was for marinade and we used apple cider vinegar because I was out of rice vinegar. We put all the marinade with the chicken thighs in a 9x 13 pan and baked as per directions.
The second double batch I used rice vinegar ( after buying some) and coked it on the stove, and added a couple of Tbsp cornstarch and it thickened up nicely. 
The first marinade was tasty and sweet, I am sure the chicken juices helped also.  The second marinade looked better and had a better texture but tasted a bit vinegary. Maybe I didn't cook it long enough? I didn't find either one spicy. Sweet and sour were the main flavours.
Next time I will follow the reviewers suggestions who said not to do a double batch of sauce, but will cook the chicken alone,  add the marinade to the other half of the sauce and then thicken it. I will also use at least half apple cider vinegar.

This was SO delicious, and not too greasy/oily like chicken thighs can tend to be. I served it with fried rice and my family loved it. This was very easy to make on a weeknight. I love it when things spend a little time in the oven so I can prep my sides.

I did just a couple of things differently. I substituted balsamic vinegar for rice vinegar, and I roasted my chicken in a cast-iron skillet that has raised grill marks, so the chicken was slightly elevated out of the oil. (Some reviews said the recipe was too oily, but mine was perfect.)

text:
This is a wonderful recipe! I make it ALMOST as written, except, when I make it, I use half the sauce to marinade this meal (put all in a large ziploc bag) and save the other half for another meal. Then, I just put the chicken into a pan, pour in all the sauce with it, and bake as directed. The sauce is AMAZING on rice and this gives plenty, no need to double this recipe at all (in fact, imo, it can be halved.) Oh, I do use only about 1-2 teaspoons of the hot sauce (NEVER 3 tablespoons, this would kill some of my diners) and use half sesame oil and half peanut oil. Anyway, an absolutely delicious dinner!

I made this last night served with Jasmine rice and fresh green beans that I cooked in with thighs and sauce the last few minutes.  It was quick and easy to make and was an excellent change from my everyday chicken.  Even my boyfriend who is very picky had seconds!  The only changes I made was-I used regular chili sauce, I did not have the "Asian chili Garlic sauce", and I used a dutch oven on stove top-first crisping the chicken then simmering covered with the marinade from the bag (I only let the chicken marinade for about 20 minutes).  The sauce was excellent and I can't wait to try it with other things. Boyfriend would like to try it as a dipping sauce for popcorn chicken...
